text:
Tried a healthier version of this soup (down from 60 grams of fat per serv. to 8!!) Cut out the butter completely (we didn't even miss it amazingly) used 6 cups of 2% milk, reduced fat sharp cheddar, reduced fat sour cream.  Reserved a 1/4 cup each of sour cream and cheese plus all of the bacon crumbles & used 1tbsp each to top each serving. DELICIOUS - never would have thought it healthy!  I also used about 6 potatos and coursley mashed them as opposed to cubed. YUM!

text:
I read every review only because I believe that even experienced cooks can always learn something. Some people complained that the soup was bland. At first taste, while it was still in the pot, I agreed. It tasted like soupy mashed potatoes. I added garlic and onion powder, parsley and cayenne pepper for some zip. When I initially viewed the recipe I felt that there was way too much butter/flour. I cut both back by half, not only to cut down on the fat, but because other reviewers stated that the soup was too thick. You definitely don't need all that roux to make this soup thick. If you do want it thicker, just add more potato, if you want it thinner, add more milk or chicken broth. This is the kind of recipe that you can put in whatever spices, herbs or meats that suit your own taste. You really can't ruin it. Overall, it was very good.

text:
Fantastic!! Better than any potato soup I've had in a restaurant and definitely my fav soup ever!! I have done a bit of tweaking to suit my own tastes.... sub 2 cups chicken stock for 2 of the cups of milk, instead of green onions I add a finely chopped yellow onion and 2 cloves garlic that I've lightly browned in the bacon grease. I mash the potatoes a little bit with fork as well, cut the sour cream down a bit, save about half of the cheese and all of the crumbled bacon to top the soup with. It's even more flavorful and thick the next day.  If it gets too thick I just add a little milk when reheating.

text:
This recipe does have potential, I wish I could omit the star rating, but that feature no longer works.  I tried this recipe exactly, but it was bland and had a thick flour taste.  My hubby said it reminded him of the paste from when he was in grade school.  If this sits for any length of time it becomes similiar to mashed potatos..  For all of you who said it was "bland" or "milky", try omitting 3 cups of milk and instead, cook half of your potatos in 3 cups of chicken broth.  Puree those, but bake the other half of the taters and cut them in small cubes.  Add you milk to the tater puree and heat to a simmer, you should not need the roux, potatos are a natural thickener.  I would recommend adding some salt, garlic powder and maybe even some chopped onion to the broth before you cook the potatoes, for added flavor.  Continue with the recipe ingreadiens and enjoy.

text:
Made this for use in bread bowls and was perfect!  Comfort food all the way.  I did add a couple cubes of chicken boullion and 2 cloves minced garlic for flavor.  Also, just a little FYI when making a potato soup....if you salt the soup at the END as opposed to during cooking, the salt flavor will be stronger.  Potatoes naturally soak up salt, so you can salt and salt while it's cooking and you'll always come out with a bland soup. Try it, I promise it will be better!

text:
Excellent and easy Baked Potato soup! One of the best I have tried. I read reviews and did a little tweaking of my own. For more flavor I sauteed 1 yellow onion in the butter and added bacon grease drippings too. I also threw in some minced fresh garlic about 3 cloves and sauteed all that together. Then I added the recommended flour. Not lower in fat but definitely adds the flavor. I did switch the 7 C. Milk, to 4 cups organic chicken broth and 3 cups milk. I also only used 1 cup of sharp cheddar and saved the rest to serve on top. The only other tweak I did was to puree half the soup before adding the bacon, sour cream and cheese. It give is a real nice texture, not too chunky and not too smooth. Better that your Houston's Restaurant too! Will definitely add this one to the recipe box!

text:
I made this yesterday and it was a HUGE hit! It tastes even better than the soup at my favorite restaurant. My husband asked me to make it again tomorrow. The only thing I did differently was I used 6 potatoes instead of 4. Very filling..and very tasty. I highly recommend.
ETA: A few more things I do differently: I use butter instead of margarine. I salted (needed quite a bit of salt) and peppered the potatoes before adding them to the soup. Once I add the potatoes to the mix I use my masher and give them a few rough mashes to thicken it up. Instead of cooking bacon I buy the already cooked kind and heat it up in the microwave - tastes the same. As for the cheese I use a bag of mild cheddar which is roughly 2 cups instead of the 1 1/4 cup the recipe calls for. This is my husband's favorite!

This is third time making this and an updated review... This was yummy! I scaled mine to 3 servings. I made mine Gluten Free by skipping the roux, which eliminated the butter. So I started with 2 cups of milk, then added the potatoes and green onions, seasoned with salt, pepper, and garlic. Next I mixed 1.5 cups of milk with 3 tsp of corn starch and added that to the soup. Turned it up to come to a boil, stirring constantly, then lowered the temp and followed the remained of the recipe. Topped with additional chives, cheese, and bacon and it was yummy! Hubby loved it!

text:
I LOVE potato soup and this one is a winner!

I made it as written, but with two small changes. FIrst, margarine? PUH-LEASE! Butter, baby. The second was unintentional but I think it made an improvement based on some of the negative reviews.  Some are mentioning that it came out mushy. Well, I cut up the potatoes and threw them in there without cooking them first. I like my potato soup to be more like chowder - thick and chunky - and that seemed to do the trick.

I am terrible at making gravies and roux, but take your time and put only a bit of flour in at a time. Then, be sure to add the first 2 cups of milk slowly, stirring it in well as you go. You can then add the rest of the milk and you'll get a nice base for the soup.

Two suggestions. First, it was a little thicker than I would like it actually, so I might thin it with a little chicken broth next time. It was also a bit more peppery than I like it - and I like pepper. I might cut it down by half and let people add it to their taste. I will likely add a bit of yellow onion next time. Not a lot, just enough to give it a smidge of onion flavor before adding the green onions at serving time.

Overall - excellent and EASY even for the roux challenged like myself. I will be making this one often for sure!

WOW! The soup was so rich, delicious and very filling. :)
Followed the reviews of others - ie: Added 2/3 packet of powdered Hidden Valley Ranch dressing, onion & garlic powder and cayenne for a kick. Added all this plus salt & pepper at the end. Found it needed quite a bit of salt.  
In addition, used 6 potatoes and the reviewes of someone else - baked 3 in the microwave and then cubed them with the skins on, peeled 3 and cubed and boiled them. 
We used 1% milk, non-fat sour cream, substitute 1 cup chicken broth for one cup of the milk and used low fat cheese. 
PS - Best of all, we got 5 servings out of this at about $2.00 per serving!

text:
Absolutely the best potato soup I've ever made.  I did follow some the of other users suggestions.  I cooked the roux a little longer than called for and I used 4 cups of half-and-half and three cups of milk.  I also used yukon gold potatoes and didn't peel them.  I used a small sweet onion and the leafy tops of four celery stalks, both of which I sauteed in butter.  I added 2 teaspoons garlic powder, 2 tablespoons chives, 1 tablespoon parsley, and about 3 cups of cheese.  I also added a can of chicken broth during the thickening stage just because I thought it would need more liquid.  It came out extremely thick and rich, almost a chowder more than a soup, but everyone loved it.  They said it was very filling and flavorful.

5+ Stars! This soup is delicious. My husband who won't eat ANYTHING with sour cream even loves it. I like to chop up a yellow onion (about 3/4 cup) and saute it with the butter in the beginning. Then I add a few green onions for the color in the end. I also add extra cheese. Make sure you leave plenty of time for prepping. Between the skinning of the potatoes, frying the bacon and chopping everything up, it takes a little longer than expected. It is worth it though! Also, be sure to use SHARP or even extra sharp cheese for a good zing!

This soup is SO GOOD and relatively easy to make. It took a long time for me to prepare because I was so paranoid about scorching the bottom that I used lower heat to bring to a boil. text:
I tweeked this recipe with what I had and it turned out GREAT... I only used 1/3 c of flower and it was plenty thick. I used two 14 oz cans of chicken broth and 3 c of 2% milk. I chopped up a small yellow onion and 4 cloves of garlic and sauteed them in the bacon grease and added. I did not have cheddar cheese so I used 14 slices of American and 1/3 of a small container of chive and onion cream cheese (it gives amazing flavor) and then added salt, pepper, basil, oregano, and a little paprika. I had 5 baked potatoes (I rubbed with olive oil and sprinkled salt, oregano and basil on them before baking). I LEFT THE SKIN ON and cubed 3 and smashed up two. This makes it a good consistency while leaving some hearty chunks.  Hope this helps!

Well the end product came out good but I had a few issues....I did not know (as it did not state) whether or not you needed to COOK the potatoes before or not.  It said large baked potatoes, I figured that means those big russett types, it didn't say you should actually bake the potato, so I have no idea what the actual recipe called for.  I actually used a 3 pound bag of organic yellow potatoes, peeled, chopped (and I had no idea, so threw them in raw), so this whole recipe took a while to cook through.  I used butter (margarine is toxic to your system, and I can't stand the taste, butter all the way).  For the milk, I used whole milk.  I didn't use green onions, I took one regular onion chopped, and a clove of garlic, browned in some butter in a pan then threw it in the pot.  The rest of the recipe I followed, it came out SO tasty.  Everyone loved it.  I made this in my Le Creuset dutch oven.  I also saved a few slices of super crispy bacon for the top, crushed once I put the soup in a bread bowl.

text:
I tweaked this recipe a bit, so it is not really this recipe anymore, but I did use it as the base.  I included the bacon fat with the butter, and then added about 1 cup of chopped celery and then cooked that until tender.  I also heated the milk.  I added 5 cups of warm milk, and then 2 cups of chicken broth.  Make sure to cook the mixture a while after adding the milk, it will take the starchy taste out.  All in all, it was a good recipe, but you can add much more flavor with the bacon fat and celery.  With these additions, I would say it is very similar to Outback Steakhouse potato soup recipe.  Very good!

text:
We added a packet of powdered Hidden Valley Ranch dressing and would probably add two next time. In addition, we used 6 potatoes. We baked three in the microwave and then cubed them with the skins on. We peeled three and cubed and boiled them. The boiled cubes retained a bit more of their shape while the baked ones mixed into the soup more. I would suggest getting some extra sour cream for garnish (we neglected to think of this).

It's pretty high in fat \but there's plenty you could do to the recipe if that stuff matters to you. Use 1% milk, low fat sour cream, substitute chicken broth for half the milk, use low fat cheese, use turkey bacon, etc.

text:
I made the recipe for 2 servings. (My husband doesn't like mashed potatoes.) I used 5 Fingerling potatoes, low fat sour cream, 1% milk, and non hydrogenated margarine. I also took advice from another review and added garlic powder. I didn't have any bacon, so I used bacon bits. I didn't cook the potatoes ahead of time. Instead I followed the directions without cooking them. I cut the potatoes in half then cut them in 1/2 inch pieces. They softened, but not enough to break up and become mashed. I also added more sour cream, and used Cougar Gold Cheese, it's a very sharp cheese you can buy online. The flavor was great! I gave this recipe 4 stars because without adding your own flavoring, it's bland.

text:
Really the best potato soup I've had- homemade, restaurant, you name it.  My 7-year-old daughter even said it was better than my mother-in-law's!

The soup can be thick, especially when warming up leftovers, but as other reviewers said it's easy to correct if you prefer it slightly thinner.

This is a very easy and FORGIVING recipe.  I messed up the roux and got it too thick before putting in the milk (like Play-Doh!) But with a little whisking, gentle heat, and patience, it smoothed out perfectly.

I prefer a real thick potato soup. So my small twist on the recipe is once I put the potatoes in I grabbed a masher and went after it until the potatoes were broken up smaller.  This really thickened it up.

NOTE that the soup *will* thicken as it cooks and especially after you remove it from the heat. So don't worry if it seems thin.

country:

text:
As written it would have been very bland but here's what I did differently.
1)I cut back on the roux like many others but found myself adding cornstarch and water to make up the difference.  Next time I'll leave the roux as is.
2)I used almost 2 pounds of small red potatoes instead of the 4 large ones.  I  also boiled them because I was in a hurry.
3) I used half chicken stock and half milk.  7 cups just seemed like a lot of milk.
4) I used much more salt and pepper than called for.  I also added cayenne pepper, basil, onions, and  4 garlic cloves for flavour.
5) I used a little velveeta and chedder mixed.
6) I left the potatoes cubed and used my hand blender to mash the potatoes after the soup was  cooked.  This way I got the consistency I wanted.
7) I added the sour cream last and only combined it.  This way I got maximum flavour from the sour cream.
8) I skipped the bacon because I don't like it.  Used white onion instead of green.
9) Lastly, I cooked the roux for a little bit.  Those who find their soup is a little "floury" it's because the flour didn't get a chance to cook.  Give the roux a couple of minutes  on the  stove over a low heat to cook the flour taste out.  It'll make a difference.
Hope that helps!  Great soup!!!

text:
Really tasty recipe. I read a handful of reviews prior to making this and am surprised no one mentioned adding an acid to the recipe.  I didn't realize it until I tasted it... only the salt is working to bring the flavors through to your tastebuds. It needed some acid and something bitter to truly make the most of the ingredients. I squeezed a quarter of a lemon in there at a time until it reached my liking (ended up at 3/4 of a lemon but would have been fine at 1/2). For the bitter aspect, I added a dash of cayenne. You can't taste the cayenne, but you'll notice more flavors revealed. 
A tip for the potatoes, I peeled and cubed them for faster cooking.  I put them in a 9x13 and covered with foil, then roasted at 400 for 30 minutes.  Check them to see if they mash easily, if they don't, throw them back in the oven for a little longer.

This was fantastic! I did make a couple changes after reading some reviews saying it was bland. I replaced 2 cups of the milk with chicken bouillon (made from granules) and since it's going right to my hips anyway, I used butter instead of margarine. This was so easy and so delicious. My daughter requested the recipe be added to her 'off to college' cookbook.  TIP for easy bacon: lay bacon slices in single layer on cold cookie sheet (with a rim), not touching, and place in COLD oven. Turn oven to 400 degrees and set timer for 17 minutes. Perfect bacon every time. Remove to paper towels to drain. Sometimes takes a minute or two more, depending on bacon thickness.

city:

text:
I love a good baked potato soup recipe, but this isn't quite it.  First, you don't need even half of all that bacon, margarine or milk.  And let's face it, this particular potato soup recipe has the word "baked" in the title.  So bake those potatoes, cool them and start making soup later in the day.  When I bake the potatoes, I also bake some leeks, halved lengthwise, one whole leek for every large potato.  Then everything cools while I make a very thin bechamel sauce out of milk and chicken broth in equal parts (2 cups liquid to every large baker), a little bacon grease and flour, and some cheddar cheese.  You're looking for just a hint of cheese flavor, not a lot.  Then I liquify the baked leeks and half the (peeled) potatoes with a hand blender, stir in the cubed baked potatoes (with some skin) and then start playing with the other flavors we all love about a baked potato.  Chives, bacon bits, green onions, sour cream or Greek yogurt, depending on your preference.  This version really comes together at the end, when you add the "stuff".  Tasting for salt is a must at this point.   But the base flavor should echo a baked potato, and you can't imitate that by boiling them.  If you want a good, quick potato soup, then yes, boil away, this recipe will please you.  But if you are looking for the flavor of a baked potato, you have to actually bake the potatoes.  It's not a huge extra step, it just requires a bit of thinking ahead.  You'll be glad you went to the bother.

text:
I'm giving the base of this recipe 5 stars, but it's really my modifications that make it a 5 (in my opinion).  I read the reviews below and took some ideas from others. I try and eat light so I tweaked this to cut some calories.  I used only a 1/2 stick of unsalted butter, 3 cups FF milk, 4 cups chicken stock or broth (I've done both), omitted the sour cream completely, and added garlic salt or powder. If it's still too thin I add a little more flour or corn starch. Because I used unsalted butter I did add a little bacon and a little cheese to add salt and thickness to the soup.  Bacon, cheese and scallions were used as a topping for whomever wanted extra. I've made it twice now and my husband even has rave reviews- that's saying a lot!!! I too think it's better the second day.  If it gets too thick I just add in a little milk when reheating.

text:
A perfect choice for a chilly night in Wisconsin!  Because several reviewers mentioned this needed more flavor (and I felt it would need a nudge, too, for our tastes), I used some diced sweet onions and a clove of garlic which I sauteed in the bacon drippings until soft.  I also added a shredded carrot.  Once that mixture was cooked, I added cayennne and smoked paprika with the flour, and then used 5 cups of milk and 2 cups of chicken stock.  I also used chives instead of green onions as that's what I had on hand and gold potatoes, again what I had on hand.  I used a freshly shredded, sharp, white cheddar.  We enjoyed this very much with the changes I made, and I will make again.

Loved this - but made it gluten and dairy free.  Instead of using flour as a thickener or milk as the liquid, I used an extra potato and 2 cans of lite Coconut Milk.  It made 5 servings.  One more can of Coconut milk would've made an additional serving.  Also, I let individuals add sour cream at the table when served rather than putting it in the entire pot.  It was awesome!  If you've never used coconut milk before - don't be afraid as the soup will be richer without a coconut taste.  And, it's better for you!

text:
What a great way to use up leftover baked potatoes!! I cooked the bacon as directed, then carmelized a whole medium diced onion adding minced garlic when it was close to being finished. Cut the margarine and flour in half, the starch from the potatoes will thicken this soup even further.  It is a little on the bland side as other reviewers stated, but play with a few of your favorite seasonings and you'll end up with a delicious, economical soup.  I ended up adding a tad more sour cream, seasoning salt, and a splash of Worcestershire sauce - yummy and hearty. Garnish with additional bacon crumbles and shredded Cheddar.  Thanks for the recipe, Sherry!!

This is a great recipe, but I did make a few adjustments.   First off, I did not have any green onions, so I sauted one regular onion with a large clove of garlic in some olive oil, then added it when the recipe called for adding onions.  For liquid, I used 3 cups milk and 3 cups chicken stock, then added more stock as needed to adjust the thickness.  I only had uncooked potatoes, and I simply added a few more minutes for the potatoes to cook.  I also left the skins on.  And due to family tastes, I left the bacon and sour cream on the side.   But the flavors were outstanding, and I thought this was a great base recipe to start from!

Awesome!  Thank you for the recipe. I made some alterations, although I'm sure the original is just as good.  Here are my changes:  1 small onion, diced (just because I don't keep green onions on hand), 50/50 split of margerine and bacon drippings (just for extra bacon flavor), for the broth I used 50/50 split of skim milk and chicken broth (made from chicken boulion - just to save some pennies), no salt (because the boulion and bacon drippings add enough sodium).  I made it ahead and then kept it warm in my crock pot on low until we were ready for dinner.  Leave your diet at the door and just enjoy some comfort food for the evening!

This soup is amazing!!  I made this on a cold evening when we had company over...and there wasn't a spoonful left!  After reading quite a few of the other reviews, the only alteration that I made to the recipe was instead of 2/3 cup butter, I used 1/3c butter and 1/3c of the bacon grease...it sounds kind of icky, but the flavor of the soup was unbelievable!  And, if you cook the butter/grease and flour for a minute or two (stirring constantly) after it starts to bubble you will loose the "floury" taste that others have talked about.

text:
Awesome recipe. I was searching for a recipe like the one my mom made when I was a kid and this has to be it. I doubled the recipe because it's winter time here and it won't go to waste with the cold weather abounding. I add green onion, white onion, cheese and celery to it too but that is just my personal preference. I recommend adding the potatoes at the very end if they are rather soft from overbaking the night before-like mine were:) Potatoes heat up quickly and retain heat for a long time so the warmth of the soup will heat the potatoes to piping hot in just a matter of minutes. Also, be careful with your salt, potatoes retain a heavy amount of salt(in fact if you ever put too much salt in a soup or such, you can add diced potatoes and strain them out after an hour or so and they will have absorbed most of the salt so you can start anew). You may think your soup isn't salty enough while cooking if your potatoes are in-just because they will absorb the salt out of the rest of the soup. But as the flavors begin to meld together, the salt will redistribute and mingle with the other aspects of the soup, especially the next day!

text:
I made this soup for this morning for dinner tonight.  It was really good and my family enjoyed it a lot.  I did make a lot of changes though.  As per previous reviewers, I reduced the margarine and flour to 1/4 c each, added about 1 tsp bacon grease and did a medley of carrots, celery and onion (each about 3/4 c) and sauteed them in the margarine before adding the flour.    I saved the bacon crumbles, cheese and sour cream for serving.  I used a lot of chicken broth and only about 2 cups milk.  At first I didn't add enough broth and as the soup cooled it got way to thick...I added about another 2 cups broth and it was the  best consistence for us.  It reheated well too.

text:
OK, it bugs me when people rate a recipe but they change everything about it. I did do that here so I apologize. I give this recipe 5 stars because it gave me some new ideas...
First,peeled and pierced the potatoes and microwaved them.
Second, sauteed half of a chopped up white onion in butter.
Third, added the flour and milk..don;t think I needed to do that. Will omit the next time.
Fourth, added in the diced up potatoes into the milk. I did not add all the milk..just kept adding as it thickened and toward the end.Also added two cans of low sodium chicken broth.
Fifth, mashed the potatoes with a masher so it had little chunks.
And finally, did add the sour cream and used another reviewers super suggestion to add the salt add the end.Doing that at the end was perfect. Added pepper in the beginning and it needed alot--I also used more potatoes.(yukons)
Thanks for helping me find a better potato soup!!

text:
This soup was absolutely delicious!!I made it on a very cold day, and this thick, hearty soup warmed me and my family up. Instead of using green onions, I used chives( it made it more like a baked potato). I would suggest using more milk if you don't like such a thick soup, like me. Also, you need to keep your eye on the soup while the milk and roux are cooking because the milk could easily burn if you're not stirring and watching it constantly. Great with thick sourdough bread! Make sure you have all your ingredients lined up and ready to go in to the soup before you begin cooking. I had to sprint back and forth doing all of the steps by myself at the same time! Very simple recipe, and quite easy to make if you only have a bit of time!

This was an okay soup, but as is I don't think I would make it again. I add my agreement to the reviewers who have said it is bland. By nature, potato soup IS somewhat bland, so that isn't the end of the world, but there isn't enough "potato" flavor and that's where the bland factor is a problem. I really wanted to like this soup better because it is a great combination of flavors. I think I will play with the idea on my own, maybe cooking some potato in the milk and then pureeing before thickening with the roux.

text:
We really enjoyed this recipe! I followed previous suggestions and didn't make the roux as thick... I doubled the basic recipe but only did 1/2 c ea of flour and butter.  (I'd say I used this recipe more as a guideline than followed precisely, don't be afraid to experiment) To add some flavor, I used some chicken broth in place of some of the milk and then added a whole bar of cream cheese before I put the potatoes in.  I think the best thing I did was fried the bacon in the same pan I made the soup in, draining the bacon grease before I made the roux and then added some bacon in with the cream cheese.  I used hash brown cubes that I'd pre-cooked in the oven to make it easier.  Everyone really enjoyed it, it wasn't overly salty but had a good flavor.  I let each person add their own sharp cheddar cheese and fixins and served it with hot crusty French Bread and a salad.  Be forewarned, it requires almost constant attention and stirring to make sure it doesn't burn in the bottom of the pan so have everything ready and waiting... Then ENJOY!

this is the best potato soup recipe i've ever tried as well as the best potato soup i've ever had. it is one of my husband's favorites. he asks for it all the time. some suggestions: be sure to cook the roux constantly, from the time you combine the butter and flour. one time i took it off the heat to combine and blend the flour to prevent it from burning and the finished soup wasn't half as good. also, be sure not to use too much sour cream. if you do it makes the soup too bland. excellent recipe. thanks!

text:
I made some minor modifications: I used 4 cups of chicken broth + 4 cups of whole milk rather than 7 cups of milk that is prescribed; I did not use the sour cream; I added several chopped up stalks of celery; I used real butter instead of margarine and I used regular yellow onion rather than green onion. The soup turned out great! The flavor and consistency were very good. I don't eat pork so I used turkey bacon rather than pork bacon. My only suggestions are: 1. Use the bacon as a garnish on top of the soup at the time that it is served so that it stays crunchy; and 2. Use more potatoes than the stated four (it needed about 2-3 more potatoes in my opinion).

text:
I liked this but after reading lots of recipes & reviews decided I wanted to go 2/3 of the broth cream base & the other 1/3 a stock base, I went with vegetable stock since Im vegetarian. I sauteed 1 cup of diced white onion in the butter then added the flour for the rue. To the broth I added a small bay leaf which is a must for any soup just dont put too much, its another subtle layer of flavor so people dont take a bite & go ok, ya, milk & potatoes, bleh ^_^  I had russet & golden yukon laying around so I tossed the russets in then waited 15 min & through in the yukon golds so the russets boiled away to thicken & flavor the broth & the yukon stayed firm enough to give you little bites of potatoes in your spoon. Topped with the cheddar & green onions & sour cream. Yum!

text:
I made this as the main dish for a party figuring it would be good to keep in the crockpot as well as filling, plus I could prepare in advance and then have no worries during the party.  I tripled the recipe.  This really is an excellent recipe but I did think it was a bit bland.  After tasting it, I looked at reviews and followed another reviewers suggestion and added ranch seasoning packet to the soup.  That made all the difference in the world.  However, you MUST be careful.  The dairy ingredients in this will scorch / brown rapidly.  If you keep it in a crockpot only keep it on warm, and don't even try to keep it on low on the stove.  Just a hint.  I will definitely make this again but not to sit out and keep warm.  It was still really good a little browned but at its best first made.

This Baked Potato Soup was great!  I did make a couple of adjustments like the other reviews suggested.  1) I used 1/2 of butter and flour.  2) I used 3 1/2 cups of skim milk and two cans of Campbell's low sodium chicken broth.  3) Used 3 large potatoes and 6 green onions.  4) I used 3 Knorr Chicken Bouillon cubes and I did not add any salt.  6) I used fat free cheese and sour cream to cut down on the fat and calories.  My soup was awesome.  I had a ton left over to last the week while the cold weather is coming through! :-)

text:
Loved the recipe but made a few tweaks. The recipe as is will easily make 8 BIG servings. I cut back to a "half" size and still fed 3 adults, and have two servings left over. Following some of the other users recommendations I made the following changes. 1. I did use all of the grease from the bacon (mmmm... bacon grease) 2. Instead of doing all of the milk. I split it with half chicken broth, half milk. I also added a cube of chicken bullion to add some flavor. 3. I added one tablespoon of Worcestershire sauce. Gave it a nice flavor! 3. I sauted 1 teaspoon minced garlic and just under 1/4 cut of minced sweet union in the butter before making the roux. 4. Lastly. I MASHED 1/3 of the potatoes to give it a thicker, almost chowder like soup. All in all... it was excellent.

Read all reviews.  Made roux w/ 1/2 of butter and recipe amount of flour.  Browned roux (dark gold color).  Sauteed 1/2 yellow onion and 2 cloves of garlic in other half of butter. I thought this would be too pasty with that much flour and butter, so I used my standard 2 Tbsp of each for the roux, and I used a mix of 2% milk and skim (cleaning out the fridge!), probably totaling closer to 5 cups of milk.  For flavor, I added a clove of garlic, some chives and used Italian truffled salt.  On a cold and blustery day like today, this was heaven in a bowl!  Even with the lighter milk, you can still get a thick enough soup but just simmering it a bit longer.  I also left my peels on the potatoes - that might not appeal to many people, but I like it that way.

region:

country:
None
text:
I use this as a base but change things up quite a bit. I start by slicing potatoes thinly and bring to a boil. While that's working I cook about 10 strips of bacon. I strain the potatoes and return most to the pot and add milk and butter and use imersion blender to smooth. To soup, add sliced carrots and small broccoli florets to add nutients. Once bacon is cooked I add diced brown onions to bacon droppings and saute. In soup I add more milk as necessary, then add shredded chedar cheese, and remaining potato pieces to have chunks of potato in the soup. Add salt, pepper, maybe garlic powder. Serve with minced green onion and chopped bacon and more shredded cheese on top. DELISH!

text:
Very tasty! I read through the reviews before starting, so I halved the butter and flour for the roux, and I think I'll still need to add a little more milk to it when I reheat the leftovers; it does thicken up well. I didn't bother to peel and cube the potatoes (though unless I'm missing something the prep time is misleading since I don't have pre-baked potatoes around the house so I would add an hour to it), I cut them in half and used a spoon to scoop bits of potato out. I also chopped up the skin of one of the potatoes and threw it in for extra fiber -- the skin's the best part! I didn't find the need to add any extra spices, the bacon, cheese, onion, and sour cream definitely provided enough flavor. Maybe people who thought it was bland were using low-fat versions of some ingredients and that's where the taste was lost.

text:
I read a lot of the reviews here and many of them said the soup was too thick. I thought it was perfect but maybe that's because I used 1% milk instead of whole milk. I also used reduced fat sour cream because I can't tell the difference between that and regular so I might as well use low fat.   Next time I make this I want to try it with pancetta instead of bacon. I thought 1 tsp. of salt was perfect, but I increased the amount of black pepper to 1 1/2 tsp. I also added 1 tsp. of dried parsley because this herb is so great with potatoes.  I think this soup would lend itself extremely well to many different flavors, ranging from cumin to curry. I think I'm going to try a curried baked potato soup next!

text:
With my changes, this recipe deserved 5 stars! I added chopped yellow onion and 2 cloves of garlic to the melted margarine and cooked for 4 minutes. I also cut the milk and half and used chicken stock. I left some of the skins on the potatoes for added texture. Instead of shredded cheddar cheese, I cut up Velveeta into cubes. To avoid the sour cream from breaking, I added it at the end when the soup cooled down from the simmer. If you feel like the soup is too thin, you can always add instant mashed potato mix. Great soup!

I have tried this recipe twice now. The first time I made it exactly according to the recipe. No one in the house would eat it. It was very bland and the bacon was really mushy. Now after reading some reviews I made some changes. I used 1/2 cup of butter and flour, I used half the amount of pepper (more for personal taste than anything), and I cut back the milk only using 3 cups and adding 3 cups of chicken broth. I also kept the bacon to put on the top instead of cooking with it. With my changes, the soup becomes 5-stars for our family!

country:
None
text:
A very hearty soup - great for the fall!  I modified it a bit, using other reviews for guidance.  I combined 4 tsp cornstarch with 1.5 cups of whole milk in a crockpot.  After baking the potatoes and frying the bacon (only had 5 slices) - I coarsely mashed the potatoes and put all of the crumbled bacon in the soup.  I finely diced 1/3 cup of celery, 1/2 cup of white onion, and one large clove of garlic.  I sauteed the garlic and onion in the bacon grease before adding to the soup.  I added parsley, paprika, salt & pepper to taste - and then finally added 2 cups of skim milk and 1 T of butter.  I set the crockpot on medium and cooked the soup for 3 hours - stirring once in a while.  It turned out great (don't forget to top it with cheddar cheese) -yum!

I followed this recipe pretty closely, and WOW, it is good. I used 1% milk, lite sour cream, and turkey bacon in an effort to reduce the fat in this recipe. I didn't put any cheese in it at all as we don't care for it in potato soup.

I was distracted by my daughters in the beginning and almost burned the bottom of the pot!  Delicious!

I'm giving this 5 stars because it was a big hit at thanksgiving dinner.  As other reviewers said, its a little thick and to some, it tasted floury, but if you cook the roux a little bit longer, you will lose that raw flour taste, just make sure you stir all the while to keep it from burning.I also sauted the green onions (tops and scallion part) in the butter rather than dumping them into the soup raw. Oh, and honestly, I'm thinking of cutting the black pepper in half next time I make it too.  Thought a tsp. was a little much.

text:
This is a great recipe, but don't believe you're going to have this thing done in 40 minutes.... even if you already have the potatoes baked!  Depending on what kind of pots you are using (stainless steel, hard anodized, ceramic, etc...) you will most likely have to take your time.  The first time I made this, I used a stainless steel stock pot, and it came out GREAT.  The second time, I was using one of my mothers old ceramic stock pots, and I scorched the milk.  I was very upset about this, but live and learn. 

But with all that aside, this truely is a great recipe, and I really wish I had the time to make it more often.

Very good and easy.  Almost as easy as opening a can of soup, but WAY better and not "canned" tasting.  I did not add the bacon to soup, but rather placed the add-ons on top. I love sour cream, but I didn't use it in this recipe. Instead of mixing the bacon in the soup, I crumbled it on top when serving in bowls. Fabulous!!!  I had to add this to my recipe box.  This is extremely easy and tasty too.  A big hit with my son who compliments me each time I make it.  My husband is hard to please but he liked this.  Leftovers are as tasty if not better and my friends found it very satisfying, tasty and warming on the cold day after a (dog) show.

I made this for my family last night and they just ate it up!  This is a nice hearty & thick soup.  I reduced the butter and flour to 1/2 cup each and kept the milk at 7 cups and it was still thick.  I cut up and boiled the potatoes until just tender instead of baking them.  I didn't add the green onions, cheese, sour cream and bacon to the soup while cooking but added them in the individual bowls.  It makes for a nice presentation adding a dollop of sour cream and sprinkling the green onions, cheese and bacon on top.  I thought the bacon might get soft in the soup.  I did add more salt than the recipe called for...maybe because I used unsalted butter.  I will definitely make this comforting soup again!!

I also used 13 potatoes, yes this was alot of potatoes BUT it gave the soup great texture.  I also omitted the onions but used onion powder instead, my husband doesn't like onions. This is a recipe you can not walk away and allow to cook on its own, it can ruin very quickly if left unattended. This is definately a keeper, restaurant quality.  Thanks Sherry!!!!

text:
Wonderful hearty soup.  Had to add approx 2 extra cups of milk it was so thick.  And now that it has sat for 3/4 hour, i find i will have to add another cup or two when i heat it up tomorrow.  My modifications:  I used butter for the roux and added 1 large chopped up onion to soften before adding the flour.  Also, stirred and cooked the roux for 5 minutes before adding the milk.  At this point i added 1 tsp salt and the pepper. I used 9 medium potatoes, and 6 green onions.  And I added 4 cups of shredded medium sharp cheddar cheese.  I checked the seasonings before serving, and had to add some more salt.  My husband, who does not like soup, had 3 bowls, and said it was worthy of being served at the finest restaurant!!!  lol

text:
Previous reviewers have said that this recipe is a little bland... I agree.  Here's what I did to make it BURST with flavor!!!

I didn't want it too thick, so I cut the butter and flour in half and it is very creamy, but not thick and gooey.  Instead of regular potatoes I used the Resers pre-cut, pre-cooked Rosemary & Roasted Garlic Diced Redskin Potatoes (two packages). I added a teaspoon (or so) of diced garlic to the butter. Added a few teaspoons of chives, used 8 green onions instead of four, and added one can of chicken broth.  Also used a few dashes of onion powder, but it's not necessary.  Also used 16 slices of bacon.  Absolutely yummy!!!
I think if you skipped all the changes except for the pre-cooked, pre-cut Rosemary Garlic potatoes it would still be fantastic.  They just add the extra punch of flavor.  Great basic recipe, but it does need a few extra touches. Thanks!

country:
None
text:
I am from true DownEast Maine.  I have been making milk based chowdahs for over 42 years....learned by over 120 years or more of wisdom from my grandmother and mother who were also born in the same region that Bar Harbor/ New England clam chowder came from.   I searched to see other ways of making it to try something different for a change and tried this.  It is VERY bland.  The roux is gloppy and reminiscent of quick chowders made by cheap restaurants or canned.  Roux is not needed, use your potatoes as a thickener by mashing some and keeping the remainder in larger chunks.  You will need more potatoes but worth it.  I have never used sour cream in a chowder before and do like that addition for this. This also needs more seasoning....?celery/onion/garlic?   
My husband and I are huge foodies and appreciate other ways  of doing things along with all cultures of foods.  I typically only review when something is good...but had to review this based on the large number of positive reviews.

Notes:
* I boiled the potatoes in chicken broth (with 1t salt) and used that for half of my liquid, then slowly added this liquid to the roux. I added to this three cups of 1% milk.
* Roux was 1/4 each of butter and flour. This was plenty.
* I added the onions and one clove of garlic to the butter before adding flour
* Cheese and sour cream amounts (used light sour cream) were perfect.
* I had red potatoes on hand and used eight.

text:
I always read the reviews and then make the recipe with others suggestions.  So...I didnt make a roux at all.  It was not necessary.  I sauted half of a chopped onion and garlic in 4T butter in a Dutch oven pan.  I then poured the peeled and diced diced potatoes in the pan with the onion.   I substituted and used half milk and half chicken broth (not stock) and poured over potatoes.  I then added teaspoon of Tony Cacheres creole seasoned salt .  After simmering until potatoes were tender, I used a hand held potato masher until the  consistency came out perfect!  I  saved the bacon, shredded cheddar cheese and sour cream and added at our bowls. It wasnt too thick or too runny...just too delicious!

text:
This recipe is very good.  Several of the reviews said it was bland so I made just a few changes.

I used 5 cups of milk and 2 cans of chicken broth and a half cup of flour.  It won't thicken a lot so I put my potatoes and onions in along with a heaping teaspoon of minced garlic and a teaspoon of celery seed.  I also doubled the salt and pepper.  I put all of this in as I boiled my potatoes so that the seasons could meld.

At the end, I put mashed potato flakes in to thicken.  My 19 year old asks for this when he is home!

text:
I have made this several times now, and each time it is as wonderful as the last. Talk about comfort food! The only modification I make is that my daughters don't eat bacon, so I make it without it, and when everything else is added, I split the pot in two, add (6 crumbled slices of) bacon and let it rest for a bit so the flavor infuses. For those who love the bacon, it's best to do it in the order it's written, but for anyone in a similar predicament to mine, this is a viable option. Thanks, Sherry Haupt, for the tasty recipe!!

This was a hit.  I did lower the to 4 stars because I modified based on other reviewers' recommendations.  I cooked the bacon in my dutch oven.  I then got rid of most of the grease but left some for flavor.  I added olive oil, half a stick of butter and half a diced onion.    I used a wooden spoon to scrape up the brown bits. text:
Perfect fall soup. This was one of the best soups I've made; with the following adjustments.

May I suggest:

Peel and dice potatoes; boil until tender. Drain. 
Saute one diced yellow onion in melted butter.
Use 6 cups of chicken broth after flour.
Bring to boil.
Add bacon, potatoes. Heat.
Add 1 cup half and half, sour cream, cheese. Heat but do not boil.

text:
I really liked the texture and taste of this soup. I used the ingredients as listed except for the sour cream, hubby does not like it. There was some adjustment of liquid amount so I could get the consistency I like.  That should be expected for almost any soup, start with a little less liquid and add extra until you are happy with the finished product. The same thing goes for the salt, add a lesser amount first, cook and taste, add more and taste until you are happy.I used a hand masher to get a potato chunk I found pleasing. 

I cut the recipe in half and I am glad I did. Hubby and I had a large bowl each and there was still 2 large servings left. But, it will be gone by tomorrow!

This is a good baseline recipe for a baked potato soup, but you should never follow a recipe exactly.

I don't use a roux as suggested, instead I just use whole milk as I don't think flour has a place in this soup.

Chives are also missing from this, as every baked potato should have on it. 

White onions can also be added at the beginning as it's a soup after all.

I love the versatility with this recipe - you can add chicken, some spices, or a little blue cheese!  It's a perfect recipe for an easy meal after a busy day!  We usually pair it with Hawaiian rolls and set it up like a small baked potato bar to let everyone pick their toppings. text:
`1Few minor changes, added chicken broth to decrease thickness and a mixture of cream and milk for creamier taste. Next time we will cut the potato back a bit. We also added a sauted onion, and added the potatoes last to avoid them getting mashed. Heres our version of the recipe.

Loaded baked potato soup 

Serves 6-8

3/4 cup butter
1 package of bacon
2/3 sweet onion chopped
3/4 cup all purpose flour
6 cups of milk 1%
1 cup cream 35%
1 1/2 cup chicken broth
5 medium yellow potatoes
4 green onions chopped
1 tsp salt
1 tsp freshly ground pepper
1/4 tsp cheese bacon chive epicure seasoning
1 1/2 cups of shredded cheddar cheese
1 cup sour cream

		
* Place bacon in a large, deep skillet. Cook over medium heat until browned. Drain, crumble, and set aside. Add sauted onions until translucent.q		
* In a stock pot or Dutch oven, melt the butter over medium heat. Whisk in flour until smooth. Gradually stir in milk, whisking constantly until thickened. Stir in onions. Bring to a boil, stirring frequently.		
* Reduce heat, and simmer 10 minutes. Mix in bacon, cheese, sour cream, salt, and pepper. Continue cooking, stirring frequently, until cheese is melted. 
* Add the potatoes

I gave this recipe 5 stars but only after making some mods to it. I already had my bacon cooked up ahead of time. I melted the butter then added the flour. Added 4 cups of half and half, then 3 cups 2% milk to add up to 7 cups of milk. Whisked until it thickened, added the red potatoes (3 large cooked and chopped into 1" chunks), bacon, green onions. text:
As written, this soup is really good,  though I usually find it needs a touch more salt. I do make this a bit differently than written usually. I dice up an onion and saute in the butter until soft, then add the flour to start making the roux. I don't usually have leftover baked potatoes so I dice up raw potatoes and let them simmer in the soup until they are cooked. You do have to keep a closer eye on the soup and stir often to prevent it from sticking to the bottom of the pot. Also, if the soup is too thick, I often add 2 teaspoons of chicken base + 2 cups of water (you can also do 2 cups of chicken stock). Very rich and delicious!

After reading some reviews from other users I decided to use 4 cups milk and 2 cups of chicken stock. I also cut back on the flour as well.

For my own additions, when I added the butter to the pan I added about a cup of finely chopped celery and yellow onion. Once the onions became translucent I added the flour.

Some helpful tips, bake the bacon in the oven for crisper bacon that you can actually find in the soup. I also microwaved the potatoes while the bacon cooked.

text:
I made this recipe the first time and it was good. I had to add more salt and pepper, and a little more cheese (a personal preference, I love cheese!). The second time I made it I made some more modifications. Instead of 7 cups of milk I used 3 cups of half and half and 4 cups of milk to make it even creamier and thicker. I also found that adding the bacon into the soup softened the bacon up, so it turned chewy. I still wanted to taste the bacon in the soup but I didn't want chewy bacon. Instead of adding the bacon bits nto the soup, I used the bacon grease in the roux! It gave it the bacon flavor and I just had bacon pieces as toppings so it would keep its crunch. 2/3 cup of butter is about 10 tablespoons and 2 teaspoons, so I added 5 tablespoons and 1 teaspoon of bacon grease and 5 tablespoons and 1 teaspoon of butter into the roux to give it that bacon flavor. Overall, it is a great recipe but for me, personally, I like it cheesier, thicker, and with crunchy bacon!

region:

country:
None
text:
This has become a staple in my household.  It is so very easy to make especially after a long day of work.  I have tweaked it of course.  I use one stick of salted butter.  I also increased the milk to 10 cups so that this has the consistency of soup vs mashed potatoes.  I do not add the sour cream or the green onions to the pot, I leave those to be added by choice by whoever is eating.  Even with the bacon this can be bland.  So when I am making my roux, after adding the flour, I add garlic powder, onion powder , celery  salt, and cajun seasoning.  I add salt and white pepper to taste after adding milk.  I garnish with sour cream, green onions, and garlic flavored croutons (my daughter loves those is her soup).  
Now when I cook this I have to make an extra pot for my in laws!

NOTE: it will initially be very thin. I was concerned when I first started to make it but it thickened up. I also had to add more ingredients because it was bland; quite a bit more salt and pepper than it said,  a bit of garlic and some finely chopped white onion.

text:
This is a GREAT base of a recipe for potato soup.  I did make a few changes due to my guys liking a LOT of flavor.  First off, I doubled the recipe.  For the butter, I did use it, but I also put in some of the bacon grease.  So I did half bacon grease, half butter.  I also used gluten free flour.  Before adding the fluids, I diced 1 small onion and 3 cloves of garlic and browned these, then I added in the fluid.  Instead of all of the milk, I used half organic chicken broth and half heavy cream.  This way I still had all of the creamy goodness, but the chicken broth added more flavor.   Then I added all of my potatoes and let it thicken up.  Instead of the sour cream, I added greek yogurt.  By this time, I'm so far away from the original recipe I'm not even measuring.  I added sharp cheddar cheese, that I grated myself (so I'm not adding any additional things into my recipe).  Topped with chopped green onions when serving and it was perfect.

text:
"Don't ever make me a baked potato again. Make me THIS SOUP instead." These were the dramatic words of my teenager as she gobbled this up.

Warm, creamy baked potato in a bowl - what could be better? Like the others, I used less butter and flour, less milk, and added some veggie broth to thin it out a little. I didn't cube the potatoes but just scooped them into the roux and then used a masher to give it some good texture.

We are vegetarian so I used some Morningstar bacon on top and it tasted just like the real thing. This is a keeper.

text:
I gave the recipe three stars because I had to doctor it up a bit to get it to my liking. After following the original recipe, I changed it up a bit to my liking:

First, I parboiled the potatoes in 4 c chicken broth, while cooking the bacon in the microwave. I reserved the bacon grease (which actually ended up being 2/3 c of fat). I then made the roux with the bacon grease and flour. For my liquid, I used 6 cups of whole milk and the reserved chicken stock from parboiling the potatoes. I then followed the recipe, as directed, adding seasoning, as needed.

I am, by no means, claiming this is healthy; it's quite the opposite. However, it IS delicious. My friends & family frequently request I make this.

text:
I took others advice and left out the butter completely. Just mixed the flour with a little milk instead. Added 1/2 sauted onion and minced garlic (didnt have green onions). Used 6 reg potatoes, 4 cups skim milk, 2 cups chicken broth, some garlic powder, 1/8-1/4 tsp cayenne, handful dried parsley and kept the light sour cream, sharp cheddar, and a few bacon pieces for on top of each bowl. Absolutely delicious, tons of flavor with not much added salt. The best part is I lowed the calories to about 369 per serving.

text:
My husband and I tried this last night. We, as well as our three year old son enjoyed it and found it very tasty. I had read some reviews previously that said it was very bland, so we added some all seasoning salt, and kept adding salt and pepper until it reached a flavor of our liking. Two small complaints: we used the exact measurements of milk and flour, yet still found it to be a little thick. I guess if you like your soup that way, it would be just right, but it was just a tad too thick for us. Also, I'm by no means a chef, so when I cook I need to have ingredients and instructions dumbed down for me as much as possible so I don't misunderstand anything. I was a little disappointed to find out after I already started cooking that the potatoes needed to be BAKED. I guess I should have figured it out on my own beforehand, however, like I said, I need things dumbed down. We improvised and cut them up and boiled them in water to soften them and it turned out fine, however, I still think it should have included baking the potatoes in the instructions.

I usually don't like baked potato soup, but I loved this soup! I used low sodium bacon and crumbled it using a food processor. I baked the russets in the microwave and after they cooled I peeled and chopped them, leaving them in big chunks because they were soft. I used lactose-free milk, regular sour cream, and the green onions. The shredded cheddar had 3 kinds of cheddar cheese. I used all measurements as called for and didn't add the salt or pepper until the end, as directed. I will definitely make this again. My husband thought it would taste good with clams in it.

text:
This is a great recipe for baked potato soup. If you follow the recipe to a t, it turns out really pasty, so I added more milk to it. I didn't measure how much milk I added, but I gradually added the milk and stirred the soup until I got the consistency I wanted to get. I adding the milk after it was all done, but next time I will do it while it's still cooking. I also used butter instead of margarine.  After reading other reviews about the soup being bland, I decided to add some garlic powder, Sazon Accent, and extra salt. Also, I think it takes much longer to prepare this recipe than stated above.  Now it could be that I take too long to cook and I have 4 year old triplets, but it just seemed like it took me much longer to get it done. The soup turned out great. We all loved it. Thanks for the recipe.

text:
Changes:  used left over baked potatoes, substituted corn starch for flour; used 3 cups milk, and served the chives and bacon on the side.  For those who complain of a flour taste, flour has to be 'browned' after adding to the butter; otherwise, you end up with a raw flour taste.  I wanted a silky base, so I did not mash any of the potatoes (and another reason I prefer corn starch}  The resulting dish was a silky smooth creamy soup base with a baked potato taste that tastes very different than when using fresh potatoes. After all, the recipe probably originated from using left over baked potatoes! Thanks for sharing, Sherry!

text:
Been getting over a cold and I was craving a hot bowl of potato soup. This was the first time I've made potato soup and this recipe was simple and GREAT! I did change a few things though. I know its supposed to be baked, but instead I boiled the peeled cubed potatoes in 4 cups of chicken broth. The potatoes absorb all the flavors of the broth which makes them so flavorful! Once boiled I added that to the milk mixture (which I cut down to 6 cups of milk, since there was about 2 cups of broth remaining with the potatoes). I'm a huge garlic fan so I also added 5 cloves of garlic minced. And I ditched the sour cream. I was also craving something meaty so I added 4 beef jalapeno sausages (Hillshire Farm), grilled and cubed. It was D-licious! I will definitely make this more often on cold rainy days :)

text:
Very delicious! Couple of adjustments...
 Instead of cooking bacon in the beginning I used real crumbled bacon from Costco (approx 3/4 - 1 C.). I used a whole yellow onion instead of green (because it's what I had) and I sauteed it in the butter before adding the flour and milk.  This seems to bring out a really yummy flavor in the onion. Also, I didn't peel the potatoes.  I really like to leave the skin on my taters as I feel that it gives more nourishment and texture.
Hope you enjoy it as much as I did.  Made it for some company and got compliments.  Will definitely be my go-to potato soup recipe!!!

I made this for the first time today it turned out great after some tweaking. I didn't have the tools required to make this dish so it took some inventive cooking but it turned out to be a yummy and hearty soup. I added a bit of vegetable favouring to my flour and butter mixture about a tablespoon. I cut out the salt and pepper just because the flavouring is so concentrated. Also adds a nice colour. I also found there was too much bacon (I know right). I will use less next time. Someone suggested coarsely mashing the potatoes as well... I will have to try that next time or cut smaller cubes. Also the sour cream is not needed I didnt add any in mine and I did not miss it nor did I miss the cheese.

text:
Fabulous!  This may insult serious cooks - I am normally not an adventurous meal-maker, but I improved here.  You know those days where you just have to make do with what you have?  Here's how I made this and it was great!  I cooked an onion in 2/3 cup butter.  I added 4 cups of 2% milk and 2/3 cup flour slowly, whisking while it thickened.  As I did this, I boiled 6 peeled and cubed potatoes.  When the milk was thick (which it will be because I'm using 4 cups instead of 7), I added a 15 oz jar of 4-cheese alfredo sauce.  (I know, right?!?  I didn't have Cheddar.)  I threw in 2 big handfuls of the chewy bacon bits (the Costco kind in a huge bag) with the milk.  It's nice and thick.  Then I drained and mashed the potatoes slightly and added to the sauce.  Yummy!  Doesn't need salt because of the alfredo.  I did put about 1/4 c of this wonderful seasoning by Knorr called Caldo de Tomate...my kids wil eat ANYTHING I put this on.  Gives it the garlic, onion, chicken flavor others were adding, too.  I don't think this needs sour cream or anything else.  I'm betting it might need that last cup of milk 'cause it's pretty thick.

text:
This soup was excellent.  I made a few changes. Following another reviewer's alterations, I used 4 cups of chicken stock, 2 cups of 2% milk, and 2 cans of low fat evaporated milk.  (I think the stock added to the flavor.)  I used only a few pieces of bacon because that was all I had on hand--and I did not think the soup lacked at all.  I also used half of a red onion (which I first sauteed in some butter ) because I did not have green onions.  I added half the potatoes to the milk base, then used my emersion blender to smooth it out.  I added the remaining potatoes and onions and boiled.  (I like my soup thick with some pieces of potato.)  I think this soup is well flavored as written, not bland like some others thought.  I do recommend being stingy with the salt at the start, adding slowly until you get your desired saltiness.  Overall this soup is delicious!  My two year old licked her bowl clean.

As written, this was mediocre at best. It was very bland, so I added garlic/onion powder, lots of dried parsley, and a healthy shake of cayenne pepper. Also subbed some chicken stock/broth for about 2 cups of the milk. After modifications, it was delicious! It does make a pretty thick roux, so be aware that you might need to adjust your liquids according to taste. Perfect for a chilly night!

text:
Hmmmm.... I don't think I like this.... This soup is WAAAY too thick and chunky (i.e. too many potatoes IMHO) and quite bland. I like a nice creamy soup (yes), but this was almost like a thick potato casserole - in a bowl. There was barely any "broth" (if that's what you call it) to dunk my sourdough bread into. I did like the tang that the sour cream gave this, which is surprising since I usually don't care for it other than as a garnish. I couldn't decide b/t this soup and absolutely ultimate potato soup by Karena, so I did a little combining of the two. I sauteed a small yellow onion, 2 stalks of celery & ~ 3 T fresh minced garlic in bacon grease, threw my cubed potatoes in, s&p'd to taste, tossed all to coat & then proceeded with Sherry's directions. I did add equal amounts of fat free milk and chicken broth to enhance the flavor as others suggested (I needed to use my "about to expire" refrigerated broth) and ended up tossing half of my crumbled bacon into the soup and heating as directed. I topped my serving with the rest of the bacon, some scallions and a handful of shredded cheddar cheese. I'm going to try slow cooker creamy potato soup by ROZANRENEE as I think I will like that better. Thanks for sharing!

I made this soup at the request of a young friend who has had their jaw wired shut due to an injury, but I don't think they're going to get much of it, it's too good!   I followed all the directions, but omitted the onion at the patient's request and didn't realize the potatoes had to be pre-baked, but it only took an additional few minutes for them to cook.  I also used fat free milk and added salt and pepper to taste.  It did turn out very thick (probably because of the additional cooking time), but is easily rectified w/additional milk or water.  This will be puree'd for the patient, who needs the extra fat and calories while eating only things that will fit through a straw.  I'm adding this to my favorite soups!  Thanks for the recipe!

text:
This was a very flavorful soup. My husband and I really liked it, although I will be making it sparingly and not using so much bacon.  Hubby has high cholesterol :)
 Edit: I made this soup for the second time tonight and my kids loved it. Paired it with Irish Soda bread (with out the rasins) and it was a wonderfull filling meal.
 I did find it easier to fry the bacon in the same pot as the rest of the soup. Just cut the raw bacon, fry in the bottom of the pot, and with a slotted spoon pull the cooked pieces out when they're done. Drain the grease out and you're all set and it's one less dish in the sink.

THIS WAS AMAZING!! My granmother made soup just like this when I was little, and when I tasted this I instantly remembered that. Thank you so much for the recipe!!

text:
This was ok.  It was bland like some of the other reviews mentioned, so we smothered each serving with extra cheese, bacon, sour cream and onions, just like a loaded baked potato.  I followed the recipe except for substituting bacon fat for the butter.  I didn't peel the potatoes or mash them up all the way so it was more chunky, but by the next day the leftovers were basically just mashed potatoes.  I've had baked potato soup that was more flavorful, and this wasn't quite it.  If I decided to make this again, I would probably try one of the other Baked Potato Soup recipes on this site, or else cut the potatoes and milk in half or double the other ingredients.  By the way, if you want a great recipe with "loaded baked potato" taste, try the Baked Potato Salad I recipe on this site :)

text:
Okay, so I used all the ingredients mentioned in the recipe, but assembled the soup differently.  I didn't saute the green onions or make a roux, instead I dumped the potatoes, milk, a bouillon cube and 1/4 cup margarine in the pot, brought it to boiling and then stirred in 1/4 cup flour mixed with 1/2 cup milk.  Boy am I glad I didn't add any more flour, it was perfect in this amount.  I also used 2.5 teaspoons salt and had the green onions, bacon and cheese so we could put in as much as we each pleased.  This made a very delicious soup that was inexpensive and pretty healthy because I used low fat dairy ingredients including margarine, as well as turkey bacon!  Thanks, we both liked this and look forward to the leftovers!

text:
This was a great recipe.  I used the bacon grease instead of the margarine/butter to make the roux, and only used about 1/2 cup of the flour.  The soup was plenty thick with the smaller amount of flour.  I didn't have leftover baked potatoes, so cubed potatoes and boiled them. I put about half the cubs in the soup, and mashed the rest to make the soup more of a "slurry" with fewer actual potato chunks.  It was phenomenal...with plenty for leftovers.

text:
I am giving this recipe five stars as is, because it is absolutely delicious and the family loves it. If there are leftovers, they often thicken in the fridge but can be reconstituted with a little milk when reheated.

I have made some adaptations over time because I no longer use the recipe while cooking this, but I do think it tastes great as written.
- I peel and chop raw potatoes and boil them instead of baking
- usually omit green onions because the kids pick them out anyway
- time-permitting, keep the soup simmering for at least an hour instead of bringing to a boil
- if I do bring it to a boil, I stir CONSTANTLY, not frequently, as it frequently burns to the bottom of the pan very quickly
- garnish with a little shredded cheese, bacon, and green onions to make it pretty :)

Having never made soup before, I was a little daunted by the idea of making a roux and cooking through the thickening process, but all came out fine. I did reduce flour and butter to 1 cup each, as suggested by other reviewers; even so, this soup did come out extremely thick. I used ~ a cup more cheese (sharp cheddar) than called for, and increased salt & pepper and added both minced garlic and garlic salt, but it still came out a little bland. The bacon helped some with flavor. Also, I was happy to discover peeling baked potatoes once cooled was as easy as peeling raw onces with a knife--I expected it to be far messier/difficult.

text:
We gave this recipe 2 tries and modified it just a smidge. 
 If you're at all sensitive to dairy, don't have this with milk. It makes all the difference in not having a stomachache from the abundance of milk.  
 We've tried it using crispy bacon and soft bacon - the soft bacon wins hands down. We used half a pound and will increase it to a full pound next time!
 Lots of cheddar cheese! We sprinkle a good serving on every bowl each time. 
 It reheats well in the microwave.
 We completely omitted the green onion the second time and didn't miss it!

text:
What a fantabulous way to celebrate the first "blustery' day of the season in California!  I was searching for a recipe I could easily put together with things I already had on hand and this was it!  The best part was that it certainly didn't taste like something I made out of convenience, more like a restaraunt meal! VERY delicious! I did add about a 1/2 teaspoon more salt, and a 1/2 cup more cheddar cheese.  I also included a pinch or so of Thyme.  I love it! I'm just hoping there are some leftovers for me to enjoy tomorrow once the family is done with supper tonight! I will be sure and double the recipe next time.  The only drawback was the constant stirring.  It took me quite a bit longer than the recipe stated to have this ready for the table. Of course I started from 'scratch' (no leftover baked potatoes) and next time I will cook the bacon in the microwave as well. OH! I also added one yellow onion in place of the green onion and sauteed it till transparent in a bit of bacon drippings before adding it to the pot. Next time maybe a bit of celery for additional texture.  I'm done now!  Thanks for sharing this recipe!!
